{{Short description|List of squads for men's international team for FIFA World Cup 2022}}
{{EngvarB|date=November 2022}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=October 2022}}
The [[2022 FIFA World Cup]] was an international [[Association football|football]] tournament held in Qatar from 20 November to 18 December 2022. The 32 national teams involved in the tournament were required to register a squad of up to 26 players, including three goalkeepers. Only players in these squads were eligible to take part in the tournament.<ref name="regulations">{{cite web |url=https://digitalhub.fifa.com/m/2744a0a5e3ded185/original/FIFA-World-Cup-Qatar-2022-Regulations_EN.pdf |title=Regulations – FIFA World Cup Qatar 2022 |publisher=[[FIFA]] |date=15 December 2021 |access-date=30 March 2022}}</ref>

A provisional release list of between 35 and 55 players per national team was submitted to FIFA by 21 October 2022, one month prior to the opening match of the tournament. The release lists were not made public by FIFA. From the preliminary squad, the final list of at most 26 and at least 23 players per national team were submitted to FIFA by 14 November, 19:00 [[Arabia Standard Time|AST]] ([[UTC+03:00|UTC+3]]), six days prior to the opening match of the tournament.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Martín |first1=Alejandro |last2=Reidy |first2=Paul |url=https://en.as.com/soccer/when-is-the-deadline-for-squads-to-be-confirmed-for-the-2022-world-cup-n/ |title=When is the deadline for squad-list confirmation for the 2022 World Cup? |work=[[Diario AS]] |date=1 October 2022 |access-date=10 November 2022}}</ref> FIFA published the final lists with squad numbers on their website on 15 November.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fifa.com/fifaplus/en/articles/world-cup-qatar-2022-official-squad-announcement-32-teams |title=Official: All squads for the FIFA World Cup Qatar 2022 |publisher=[[FIFA]] |date=15 November 2022 |access-date=15 November 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://fdp.fifa.org/assetspublic/ce44/pdf/SquadLists-English.pdf |title=FIFA World Cup Qatar 2022 – Squad list |publisher=[[FIFA]] |date=15 November 2022 |access-date=15 November 2022}}</ref> The final matchday at club level for players named in the final squads was 13 November 2022, while clubs had to release their players by the following day.<ref name="regulations"/> In the event that a player on the submitted squad list suffered from an injury or illness prior to his team's first match of the tournament, that player could be replaced at any time up to 24 hours before their first match. The team doctor and the FIFA General Medical Officer had to both confirm that the injury or illness was severe enough to prevent the player from participating in the tournament. Replacement players did not need to be limited to the preliminary list.<ref name="regulations"/>

On 23 June 2022, the Bureau of the [[FIFA Council]] approved the increase of the maximum number of players included on the release list (from 35 to 55) and final list (from 23 to 26). This was due to the timing of the tournament in the football calendar and the disruptive effects caused by the [[COVID-19 pandemic]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fifa.com/tournaments/mens/worldcup/qatar2022/media-releases/bureau-of-fifa-council-approves-increase-of-fifa-world-cup-tm-squads-to-26 |title=Bureau of FIFA Council approves increase of FIFA World Cup squads to 26 players |publisher=[[FIFA]] |date=23 June 2022 |access-date=9 August 2022}}</ref>

The position listed for each player is per the official squad list published by FIFA. The age listed for each player is as of 20 November 2022, the first day of the tournament. The numbers of [[Cap (sport)|caps]] and goals listed for each player do not include any matches played after the start of the tournament. The club listed is the club for which the player last played a competitive match prior to the tournament.{{refn|group=note|This is the club a player was last able to play for during the previous season in the event a player did not play a competitive match.}} The nationality for each club reflects the national association (not the league) to which the club is affiliated. A flag is included for coaches who are of a different nationality to their team.

==Group A==

Coach: {{flagicon|ARG}} [[Gustavo Alfaro]]

==Group C==

===Argentina===
[[File:ARG Line-up - ARG vs MEX for 2022 FIFA WC.jpg|thumb|The Argentina starting XI for their second group match]]
Coach: [[Lionel Scaloni]]

[[Argentina national football team|Argentina]] announced their final squad on 11 November 2022.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.afa.com.ar/es/posts/lista-de-convocados-de-la-seleccion-argentina-para-qatar-2022ok |title=Lista de convocados de la Selección Argentina para Qatar 2022 |trans-title=Argentina's squad list for Qatar 2022 |publisher=[[Argentine Football Association]] |date=11 November 2022 |access-date=11 November 2022 |language=es}}</ref> [[Nicolás González (footballer, born 1998)|Nicolás González]] withdrew injured and was replaced by [[Ángel Correa]] on 17 November.<ref>{{cite tweet |author=Argentina national football team |author-link=Argentina national football team |user=Argentina |number=1593315253227487233 |date=17 November 2022 |title=Tras el entrenamiento de hoy, el futbolista Nicolás González sufrió una lesión muscular y quedará desafectado de la nómina mundialista. En su reemplazo, el CT de Selección Argentina, convoca a Ángel Correa. |trans-title=After today's training session, Nicolás González suffered a muscle injury and will be left out of the World Cup squad. In his place, the coach of the Argentina national team has called up Ángel Correa. |language=es |access-date=17 November 2022}}</ref> On the same day, [[Joaquín Correa]] withdrew injured, and was replaced by [[Thiago Almada]] on 18 November.<ref>{{cite tweet |author=Argentina national football team |author-link=Argentina national football team |user=Argentina |number=1593352407299153920 |date=17 November 2022 |title=El futbolista Thiago Almada se suma a la convocatoria mundialista de Qatar 2022. |trans-title=Thiago Almada has been added to the squad for Qatar 2022. |language=es |access-date=17 November 2022}}</ref>

===Mexico===
[[File:Argentina vs mexico mexico lineup.jpg|thumb|The Mexico starting XI for their second group match]]

===Saudi Arabia===
Coach: {{flagicon|FRA}} [[Hervé Renard]]

===France===
[[File:2022 FIFA World Cup France 4–1 Australia - (6).jpg|thumb|The France starting XI for their first group match]]
Coach: [[Didier Deschamps]]

[[France national football team|France]] announced their 25-player final squad on 9 November 2022.<ref>{{cite web |last=Orsini |first=Vincent |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8465-la-liste-des-vingt-cinq-pour-le-mondial.html |title=La liste des vingt-cinq pour le Mondial |trans-title=The list of twenty-five for the World Cup |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=9 November 2022 |access-date=12 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://media.fff.fr/uploads/files/36b10b99335a6db917611049430336a0.pdf |title=Coupe du monde 2022 – La liste des 25 |trans-title=2022 World Cup - The list of 25 |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=9 November 2022 |access-date=12 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref> The final squad was extended to 26 players on 14 November with the addition of [[Marcus Thuram]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8509-marcus-thuram-convoque.html |title=Marcus Thuram convoqué |trans-title=Marcus Thuram summoned |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=14 November 2022 |access-date=14 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref> On the same day, [[Presnel Kimpembe]] withdrew injured and was replaced by [[Axel Disasi]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8511-disasi-remplace-kimpembe.html |title=Disasi remplace Kimpembe |trans-title=Disasi replaces Kimpembe |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=14 November 2022 |access-date=14 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref> [[Christopher Nkunku]] withdrew injured on 15 November,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8538-nkunku-forfait.html |title=Nkunku forfait |trans-title=Nkunku withdraws |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=15 November 2022 |access-date=16 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref> and was replaced by [[Randal Kolo Muani]] on 16 November.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8540-kolo-muani-remplace-nkunku.html |title=Kolo Muani remplace Nkunku |trans-title=Kolo Muani replaces Nkunku |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=16 November 2022 |access-date=16 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref> It was announced on 20 November that [[Karim Benzema]] had suffered an injury and was not expected to play any part in the tournament; he was not replaced in the squad.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fff.fr/article/8581-karim-benzema-forfait-pour-la-coupe-du-monde.html |title=Karim Benzema forfait pour la Coupe du Monde |trans-title=Karim Benzema out of the World Cup |publisher=[[French Football Federation]] |date=19 November 2022 |access-date=19 November 2022 |language=fr}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Ducher |first=Maxime |url=https://www.leparisien.fr/sports/football/coupe-du-monde/coupe-du-monde-2022-karim-benzema-ne-sera-pas-remplace-20-11-2022-T6IH5IL6ZFHGRHQW7EPYIG5KSI.php |title=Coupe du monde 2022 : Karim Benzema ne sera pas remplacé |trans-title=World Cup 2022: Karim Benzema will not be replaced |work=[[Le Parisien]] |date=20 November 2022 |access-date=20 November 2022 [[Morocco national football team|Morocco]] announced their final squad on 10 November 2022.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://site.frmf.ma/%d9%84%d8%a7%d8%a6%d8%ad%d8%a9-%d8%a7%d9%84%d9%85%d9%86%d8%aa%d8%ae%d8%a8-%d8%a7%d9%84%d9%88%d8%b7%d9%86%d9%8a-%d8%a7%d9%84%d9%85%d8%b4%d8%a7%d8%b1%d9%83%d8%a9-%d9%81%d9%8a-%d9%86%d9%87%d8%a7%d8%a6/ |title=لائحة المنتخب الوطني المشاركة في نهائيات كأس العالم قطر 2022 |trans-title=The list of the national team participating in the 2022 World Cup Qatar |publisher=[[Royal Moroccan Football Federation]] |date=10 November 2022 |access-date=10 November 2022 |language=ar}}</ref> [[Amine Harit]] withdrew injured and was replaced by [[Anass Zaroury]] on 16 November.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://site.frmf.ma/%d8%a7%d9%84%d8%b3%d9%8a%d8%af-%d9%88%d9%84%d9%8a%d8%af-%d8%a7%d9%84%d8%b1%d9%83%d8%b1%d8%a7%d9%83%d9%8a-%d9%8a%d9%88%d8%ac%d9%87-%d8%a7%d9%84%d8%af%d8%b9%d9%88%d8%a9-%d9%84%d8%a7%d9%86%d8%b3-%d8%b2/ |title=السيد وليد الركراكي يوجه الدعوة لانس زروري للمشاركة في كاس العالم |trans-title=Mr. Walid Regragui invites Anass Zaroury to participate in the World Cup |publisher=[[Royal Moroccan Football Federation]] |date=16 November 2022 |access-date=16 November 2022 |language=ar}}</ref>

* The [[Qatar national football team|Qatar]] (hosts) and [[Saudi Arabia national football team|Saudi Arabia]] squads are made up entirely of players from the countries' domestic leagues.
* The [[Senegal national football team|Senegal]] squad is the only squad not to include any players employed by clubs in their home country.
* The [[Canada men's national soccer team|Canada]] and [[Wales national football team|Wales]] squads both include players employed by domestic clubs, but no players employed in the [[Canadian soccer league system|Canadian]] or [[Welsh football league system|Welsh]] domestic league systems. All Canadian domestic players play for Canadian teams in the American [[Major League Soccer]]; all Welsh domestic players play for Welsh teams in the English [[EFL Championship]].
* Two squads have only one domestic-based player ([[Argentina national football team|Argentina]] and [[Serbia national football team|Serbia]]).
* The [[Brazil national football team|Brazil]] squad has the most players from a single foreign federation, with 12 players employed in [[English football league system|England]].
* Of the countries not represented by a national team at the World Cup, [[Italian football league system|Italy's league]] provides the most squad members, with 70.<ref name="WaPo">{{cite news |last=Dunbar |first=Graham |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/sports/soccer/world-cup-watch-european-clubs-have-73percent-of-players-selected/2022/11/15/a754f0c2-64f7-11ed-b08c-3ce222607059_story.html |title=World Cup Watch: European clubs have 73% of players selected |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |agency=[[Associated Press]] |date=15 November 2022 |access-date=19 November 2022}}</ref>
* The second-tier English Championship has 29 players selected, though none for England.<ref name="WaPo"/>
* The lowest league on a domestic pyramid to be represented at the World Cup is [[EFL League Two]], the English fourth tier. It is represented by Welsh players [[Chris Gunter]] ([[AFC Wimbledon]]) and [[Jonny Williams]] ([[Swindon Town F.C.|Swindon Town]]).
